<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_School">Business School</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Business School">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1535" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg/180px-Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg/270px-Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg/360px-Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Business_Departments_-_University_of_Mannheim.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Mannheimer Villen</i> belong to the University and host several departments of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mannheim_Business_School" title="University of Mannheim Business School">Business School</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The University of Mannheim Business School is the undergraduate and graduate business school of the University of Mannheim. The School awards Bachelor of Business Administration, Master of Management (MMM), and Ph.D. degrees. As the first German institution, the Business School of the University of Mannheim has gained the "Triple Crown" (<a href="/wiki/Triple_accreditation" title="Triple accreditation">Triple accreditation</a>): It is accredited by AACSB International, the Association of MBAs (AMBA) and EFMD (EQUIS). With 37 chaired professors and about 4,000 students, the Business School ranks among the largest in Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1020" data-file-width="654" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg/190px-Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg/285px-Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg/380px-Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rektoratshof_UMA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rectorate's yard in the front of the Business School</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The undergraduate business degree has the most developed integrated international exchange program in Germany, with a mandatory exchange term during the third year and more than 95% of third-year class students participating. Students generally study for one semester abroad at one of more than 400 highly respected partner schools in more than 50 countries, for instance: <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a>, <a href="/wiki/HEC_Paris" title="HEC Paris">HEC Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hong_Kong" title="University of Hong Kong">University of Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Miami" title="University of Miami">University of Miami</a>. Instead of the exchange term, the program exceptionally allows students to have a further semester at Mannheim with a special curriculum focusing on international course load and business ethics.</p>
<p>Besides the strong international outlay due to the integrated exchange semester, internationality and cross-cultural learning is emphasized by obligatory language tracks in the course curriculum (Chinese, Japanese, Spanish, Russian, Korean or Portuguese tracks possible) and 70% of courses held in English.</p>
<p>At graduate level the "Mannheim Master of Management (MMM)" offers an entirely open course curriculum that allows students to choose courses according to their own wishes. The MMM can thus be converted to a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Finance" title="Master of Finance">Master of Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Accountancy" title="Master of Accountancy">Master of Accounting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Marketing_Research" title="Master of Marketing Research">Master of Marketing</a> etc. The range of available courses include all business related subjects and interdisciplinary courses, such Corporate Finance and Banking, Marketing, Entrepreneurship, Strategic Management, Operations Research or Information Systems, and many more. Furthermore, students can select courses out of the Economics, Sociology and Humanities departments.</p>
<p>Several double degree graduate programs with renowned institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen's University">Queen's University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESSEC" title="ESSEC">ESSEC Business School Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bocconi_University" title="Bocconi University">Bocconi University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Business_School" title="Copenhagen Business School">Copenhagen Business School</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a> are available and enable the students to pursue two master's degrees at the same time. International exchange programs, comparable to those at undergraduate level (while not mandatory), also allow for cross-cultural cooperation and learning. Usually more than 40% of the MMM classes each year choose to participate in one of those programs.</p>
<p>On-campus recruiters include companies like <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann" title="Bertelsmann">Bertelsmann</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JP_Morgan" title="JP Morgan">JP Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Co." title="McKinsey &amp; Co.">McKinsey &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reckitt_Benckiser" title="Reckitt Benckiser">Reckitt Benckiser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bain_%26_Company" title="Bain &amp; Company">Bain &amp; Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Consulting_Group" title="Boston Consulting Group">Boston Consulting Group</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merck_KGaA" title="Merck KGaA">Merck KGaA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Wyman" title="Oliver Wyman">Oliver Wyman</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%26G" title="P&amp;G">P&amp;G</a>, <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a>, <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a>, and many more.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Law_and_Economics">School of Law and Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: School of Law and Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Department of Law:</b></p>
<p>Eighteen full professors, their staff and numerous renowned associate lecturers research and teach at the Department of Law. The Department of Law is home to several important institutes and programs (e.g. the institute for company law (<i>Institut für Unternehmensrecht (IURUM)</i>), the institute for insurance law (<i>Institut für Versicherungswissenschaft</i>) or the centre for the law of bankruptcy law (<i>Zentrum für Insolvenz und Sanierung (ZIS)</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1322" data-file-width="2325" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg/240px-Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg/360px-Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg/480px-Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schloss_Mannheim_Durchfahrt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Westflügel</i> (West Wing) that hosts the department of law</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The department of law places clear emphasis on the fields of commercial and business law. Close ties to legal and business practice, combined with an interdisciplinary profile in the economic sciences, are hallmarks of the Department of Law.</p>
<p>Mannheim's Law school is the first law school in Germany to introduce a modern Bachelor of Law study program, the so-called "Bachelor Unternehmensjurist", while maintaining the high standards of the legal State Examination system. The programme combines modules from the Department of Law (thematic priority on business law) and the Business School (thematic priority human resources or tax and accounting). It enables students to study law and business simultaneously<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and ends after 6 semesters (3 years) with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a>. It is the first bachelor's degree in Germany which can be followed up with a master's (graduate) programme in business, a master's (graduate) programme of law or the German state examination in law (<a href="/wiki/Staatsexamen" title="Staatsexamen">Staatsexamen</a>) (German government licensing examination).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2236" data-file-width="1908" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg/210px-Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg/315px-Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg/420px-Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Verfuegungsgebaeude_Mannheim_L7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Department of Economics and GESS Graduate School</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Department of Economics:</b></p>
<p>More than twenty full-time senior faculty members and 21 assistant professors and numerous lecturers are engaged in a variety of research projects at the frontiers of their fields, ranging from micro- and macroeconomics, econometrics, labour economics, industrial organization, financial economics, auctions and game theory, policy analysis and evaluation to economic history and international trade. The department has special expertise in microeconomic specializations and econometrics, both in theory and application. Its research programmes are aided by large institutional grants from the German National Science Foundation (DFG); additional funds are obtained from other public and private institutions. The department owns a library collection of more than 350,000 volumes in German as well as other languages (mostly English) and subscribes to 400 journals.</p>
<p>The Department of Economics of the University of Mannheim is ranked 1st in Germany and is ranked as the best and most research intensive department among all German-speaking countries. Furthermore, the 2013 Economics Ranking of <a href="/wiki/Handelsblatt" title="Handelsblatt">Handelsblatt</a> ranks 6 professors of Mannheim's department among the world's 100 most influential researchers in Economics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WiWo_Ranking_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-WiWo_Ranking-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The department maintains close partnerships and exchange agreements with universities like <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a> or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warwick_University" title="Warwick University">Warwick University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Social_Sciences">School of Social Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: School of Social Sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The School of Social Sciences comprises the fields of <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a> with an academic staff of 36 professors<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and 150 additional scientists. The social sciences at the University of Mannheim have an excellent international reputation, reflected by rankings, awards and third-party funds. The faculty is well-known<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> for its empirical-analytical orientation and its focus on Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1498" data-file-width="1898" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg/220px-Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg/330px-Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg/440px-Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A4t_Mannheim_-_Geb%C3%A4ude_A5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
School of Social Sciences</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Department of Sociology</i> at the School of Social Sciences is renowned for its strength in empirical and analytical research, and for using innovative quantitative techniques in its research design.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1505" data-file-width="1260" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg/200px-Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg/300px-Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg/400px-Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uni-Mannheim_Neubau.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Glass Cube belonging to the School of Social Sciences</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Department's main areas of focus in research and teaching consist of Sociological Theory, Comparative Sociology, Stratification Research, Economic Sociology, Social Psychology, and Quantitative Research methods. The department maintains close cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Centre_for_European_Social_Research" title="Mannheim Centre for European Social Research">Mannheim Centre for European Social Research (MZES)</a> and the Leibniz Institute for Social Research (GESIS). Since 2014 the Mannheim School of Social Sciences is the first and only European partner institution of the EITM Summer Institutes and provides advancing theoretical and empirical research training in form of a <a href="/wiki/Summer_school" title="Summer school">summer school</a> to scholars, together with its US partners <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_University" title="Washington University">Washington University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Department of Psychology</i> has developed into one of the leading research and teaching institutions in Germany, focusing mainly on the research areas of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_and_Organizational_Psychology" title="Industrial and Organizational Psychology">Industrial and Organizational Psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_behaviour" title="Consumer behaviour">Consumer Psychology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_Psychology" title="Social Psychology">Social Psychology</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cognitive_Psychology" title="Cognitive Psychology">Cognitive Psychology</a>. Recently a new chair for Consumer Psychology has been established and a collaborative research center on decision making been opened. Further research is also being conducted at the Otto-Selz-Institute (Mannheim Centre for Work and Health), which focuses on the impact of negative influences at the workplace.</p>
<p>The <i>Department of Political Science</i> has an emphasis on the use of quantitative and analytical methods in its research on political phenomena. The Department's main areas of focus in research and teaching are Comparative Politics and International Relations, with emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Theories_of_political_behavior" title="Theories of political behavior">Political Behavior</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_Economy" title="Political Economy">Political Economy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Relations" title="International Relations">International Conflict</a>, and German and European Politics. The research activities of the Department of Political Science are complemented by the Mannheim Centre for European Social Research (MZES) and the Collaborative Research Centre SFB 884 "Political Economy of Reforms", The Department of Political Science was one of the first universities in Germany to introduce a systematic and international study program by offering Bachelor, Master and Ph.D (doctoral) degree programs. Furthermore, the department holds close partnerships and exchange programs with the Washington University, <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Milan" title="University of Milan">University of Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>. The University of Mannheim is editor of the <a href="/wiki/American_Political_Science_Review" title="American Political Science Review">American Political Science Review</a>, which is published by <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Press" title="Cambridge University Press">Cambridge University Press</a>. The current <a href="/wiki/Editor-in-chief" title="Editor-in-chief">editor-in-chief</a> is Mannheim's Thomas König.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Humanities">School of Humanities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: School of Humanities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B6_innen_05_(1_von_1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1831" data-file-width="1225" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/B6_innen_05_%281_von_1%29.jpg/160px-B6_innen_05_%281_von_1%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/B6_innen_05_%281_von_1%29.jpg/240px-B6_innen_05_%281_von_1%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/B6_innen_05_%281_von_1%29.jpg/320px-B6_innen_05_%281_von_1%29.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B6_innen_05_(1_von_1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Department of Humanities, in the background the School of Social Sciences is visible</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mannheim School of Humanities engages in research and teaching at the intersection of culture, society and business with an interdisciplinary, international and intercultural perspective. With 26 full professorships, two junior professorships, about 100 research and teaching associates and more than 2,800 students in total, the Mannheim School of Humanities is the university's second largest school. Each year, about 1,000 new students take up their studies at the School of Humanities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The School encompasses English studies, Germanic studies, history, media and communication studies, philosophy and Romance studies. These disciplines rank Mannheim in the top three to ten institutions in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In close cooperation with the Business School, the School of Humanities offers several renowned interdisciplinary study programs such as "Culture and Business".</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1788" data-file-width="2326" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg/240px-Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg/360px-Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg/480px-Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Universitaetsgebaeude_und_Rhenania_in_Mannheim.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mannheim School of Computer Science and Mathematics</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Distinguished fields of research are globalization studies and linguistic topics such as multilingualism. The school stands in close cooperation with the Institute for the German Language (IDS), the Mannheim Centre for Empirical Multilingualism Research (MAZEM gGmbH) and maintains extensive cooperation with a large variety of international partner universities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Computer_Science_.26_Mathematics">School of Computer Science &amp; Mathematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: School of Computer Science &amp; Mathematics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The school consists of the Institute of Mathematics and the Institute of Computer Science:</p>
<p><b>Department of Computer Science:</b></p>
<p>The Institute of Computer Science and Business Informatics consists of eleven Chairs and Professorships dedicated to Data Management, Software Development, Web Technologies, Process Modelling, and Mobile and Visual Media. Their common point of interest is the management of complex data material for society and economy. The institute is mainly located in the building A 5,6. Together with the business informatics group that are part of the Business School, the Institute of Computer Science recently founded the Center for Business Informatics to ensure that research and teaching standards in this area remain at the highest level.</p>
<p><b>Department of Mathematics:</b></p>
<p>The Institute of Mathematics consists of eleven Chairs and 22 Professorships that focus on classical mathematical disciplines as well as on economic and practical-oriented fields of mathematics. The main areas of research include Algebra, Analysis, Geometry, Stochastics and Mathematical Statistics as well as Mathematics in Finance and Insurance. Through its successful focus on business mathematics in research and teaching, the Institute of Mathematics is constantly expanding its close cooperation with the University's Department of Economics and the Business School.</p>

<td style="padding-right: 1em">10</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The University of Mannheim was called "The Harvard of Germany" by the German newspaper <a href="/wiki/Die_Zeit" title="Die Zeit">Die Zeit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Die_Zeit_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Die_Zeit-60">[60]</a></sup> Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> referred to the UMA as "Germany's leading higher education institution for business and economics" since the university is especially known for Business, Economics and Social Sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The University is widely considered to have the best business and economics program in Germany<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WiWo_Ranking_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-WiWo_Ranking-34">[34]</a></sup> and its Master in Management is ranked 14th in Europe by the FT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The university's business school is ranked 1st in Germany by the <a href="/wiki/Eduniversal" title="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</a> ranking and 34th worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Business School's MBA program is ranked globally 23rd by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNN_Expansion" title="CNN Expansion">CNN Expansion</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MBS_ranking_placements_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-MBS_ranking_placements-65">[65]</a></sup> and 26th by <a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MBS_ranking_placements_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-MBS_ranking_placements-65">[65]</a></sup> Its Executive MBA ranks 21st internationally in the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a> Executive MBA Ranking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MBS_ranking_placements_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-MBS_ranking_placements-65">[65]</a></sup> Moreover, the School of Law, the School of the Humanities, and the School of Mathematics and Computer Science – due to their close collaboration with Business Administration and the Social Sciences – provide their students with unique opportunities for specialization. According to the ranking of the German business newspaper <a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswoche" title="Wirtschaftswoche">Wirtschaftswoche</a>, which based on the opinion of 500 <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a> managers of leading companies in Germany, all programs of the university reached a place in the top 10. Moreover, a study conducted in 2011 by the social networking platform <a href="/wiki/XING" title="XING">XING</a> revealed that the majority of executives in German companies are alumni of the University of Mannheim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> According to the current edition of the CHE-Ranking, the University of Mannheim is one of the most successful German universities. Nationwide it received the best evaluation in four of its disciplines: business administration, economics, political and social science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In 2012 the university received the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ERASMUS" title="ERASMUS">ERASMUS</a> E-Quality seal for its performance in the ERASMUS exchange program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The German Academic Exchange Service (DAAD) awards this distinction annually to universities that perform especially well in the ERASMUS exchange program.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The admission process of the University of Mannheim is known as highly competitive. The Mannheim's business administration undergraduate program is the most selective undergraduate program at the University of Mannheim with an admission rate of only 10 to 11%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It is widely known for its reputation as the most prestigious undergraduate business program in Germany<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wiwo.de_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-wiwo.de-5">[5]</a></sup> and its highly selective admissions. Undergraduate as well as graduate students are generally selected based on academic excellence and extraordinary extracurricular involvement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Furthermore, students have to proof an excellent command of the English language through very high <a href="/wiki/Abitur" title="Abitur">Abitur</a> grades in English or English tests, like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TOEFL" title="TOEFL">TOEFL</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IELTS" title="IELTS">IELTS</a>. In 2012, the mean entrance average for Mannheim's business undergraduate degree was 1.2/5.0 (with 1.0 the highest grade possible), with more than 90% of admitted applicants ranking in the top 10% of their high school classes. Other highly competitive undergraduate programs at the university include Economics, <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">Psychology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Information_Systems" title="Information Systems">Information Systems</a> and Law.</p>
<p>Admission to consecutive Master's programs always requires at least an undergraduate degree equivalent to the German grade "good" (i.e., normally a B+ in American, or a 2:1 in UK terms). Furthermore, at graduate level, applicants of the Business School have to submit a <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Management_Admission_Test" title="Graduate Management Admission Test">GMAT</a> score of at least 600 to be considered in the application process while applicants for the economics programs have to absolve the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Record_Examinations" title="Graduate Record Examinations">GRE</a> with high scores - especially in the quantitative section of the test.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The average GMAT score of the class 2015 of the Mannheim Master in Management was 680.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Admission to Mannheim's full-time MBA program was rated as the most selective in Europe, on par with the <a href="/wiki/HEC_Paris" title="HEC Paris">HEC Paris</a> MBA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1572" data-file-width="1568" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg/200px-Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg/300px-Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg/400px-Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uni-Mannheim_Bibliothek.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A3 Library that primarily hosts volumes of the humanities and social departments</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_length_of_courses">Organization and length of courses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Organization and length of courses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The academic year is divided into two terms. The winter term (semester) runs from September 1 to January 31 and the summer term from February 1 to July 31. Mannheim was the first university in Germany that decided to adopt the timeframe of international academic years whereby the academic winter term already starts in September - while in Germany the classical academic year begins in October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Thus, classes are held from early September to early December and early February to early June. Students can generally only begin their studies in the winter term and not during the summer terms. The standard time required to finish a bachelor's degree is principally six semesters, and a further four semesters for consecutive master's degrees. The normal length of Ph.D. programs for full-time students is 6 semesters.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuition_fees">Tuition fees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tuition fees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In general, the German government heavily subsidizes university study to keep higher education affordable and accessible regardless of the student's <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic_status" title="Socioeconomic status">socio-economic background</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> After the German "<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Constitutional_Court_of_Germany" title="Federal Constitutional Court of Germany">Bundesverfassungsgericht</a></i>" (Constitutional Court) had overturned a federal law prohibiting tuition fees in year 2005 and devolved the right to administrate tuition fees to the federal state level, the University of Mannheim decided upon the introduction of tuition fees in the summer term of 2006.</p>
<p>Following the ruling in 2005, the University of Mannheim started charging tuition fees of €500 per semester (i.e. €1,000 per year) since the beginning of the autumn/winter term 2007. (as with any university in Baden-Württemberg) In addition to the tuition fees a basic contribution fee to the state-run <i>Studentenwerk</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> of €66.5 as well as a €60 administrative fee (<i>Verwaltungsgebühr</i>) are mandatory. Following an amendment in Baden-Württemberg students do not have to pay the tuition fees of €500 any longer from 2012 on.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_aid">Financial aid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Financial aid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2007, the University of Mannheim established a university-wide <a href="/wiki/Scholarship" title="Scholarship">scholarship</a> system addressing both undergraduate and graduate students. With more than 144 scholars in 2014 the university maintains one of the largest scholarship systems of all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_universities" title="Public universities">public universities</a> in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-81">[81]</a></sup> The University works, thereby, in close cooperation with a large number of partners and funders that include individuals, companies and foundations. Among the scholarship partners, companies like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Co." title="McKinsey &amp; Co.">McKinsey &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merck_KGaA" title="Merck KGaA">Merck KGaA</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BASF_SE" title="BASF SE">BASF SE</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann" title="Bertelsmann">Bertelsmann</a> can be found, as well as foundations like the <i>Ulrike &amp; Dr. Axel Weber Stiftung</i> or the <i>Ernst &amp; Young Stiftung</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The recipients of all scholarships are chosen based on their academic performance and for all scholarships an application is mandatory. The scholarships are both directed at enrolled/incoming students as well as university applicants. In addition to the respective funding, important networking possibilities are offered. In the academic year of 2011/12, the University integrated the Deutschland Scholarship of the Federal Government in its scholarship system. Mannheim's scholarship includes several programs:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Deutschland Scholarship</i> was initiated in the year of 2011 by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Federal_Government" title="German Federal Government">German Federal Government</a> designated as a national scholarship program supporting selected scholars with a monthly funding of €150. This base-line scholarship amount is sponsored by private donors. The Federal Government doubles this amount of funding to €300 per month. In addition to a student's academic performance, the University of Mannheim considers the applicants' personal circumstances, social commitments or extracurricular success during the assessment. The <i>Mannheim Votum Scholarship</i> was established in 2011 by the Votum-Foundation that assigns scholarships to orphans in need of support in order to enable successful studies at the University of Mannheim. All complete, semi-, <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorce</a> or social <a href="/wiki/Orphan" title="Orphan">orphans</a> are entitled to an application. The funding contains a maximum of €6,000 per year. The <i>Mannheim Sports Scholarship</i> is explicitly oriented towards students who are already enrolled at the University of Mannheim. In order to financially support top athletes at the University of Mannheim and to consider their additional effort for training and competitions, the university has established a sports scholarship. The Mannheim Sports Scholarship supports enrolled athletes way beyond the cooperation agreement "<i>Kooperationsvereinbarung/Partnerhochschule</i>" for top class sports. Organizational as well as financial support is supposed to mitigate the dual burden of top athletes – this support, for instance, include individual tutorships and assistance in administrative issues as well. The University chooses the scholarship recipients in conjunction with their private donors. Furthermore, the system aspires to a close contact between the scholarship holders and donors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1908" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg/200px-Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg/300px-Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg/400px-Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bibliothekseingang_Mannheimer_Schloss.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Entrance to the former Palace Library</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mannheim's library system's origins date back to the early 20th century. When Mannheim's City College of Trade (<i>Städtische Handelshochschule</i>) was founded in 1907, it maintained a large central library, which was supplemented by various departmental libraries. In 1932 these libraries were merged with the Municipal Palace Library (<i>Städtische Schlossbücherei</i>), which later became the Municipal Science Library Mannheim (<i>Wissenschaftliche Stadtbibliothek Mannheim</i>).</p>
<p>When the National Socialists came to power in 1933, the College of Trade was dissolved and the books in its library were donated to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Heidelberg" title="University of Heidelberg">University of Heidelberg</a>. In 1946 the bulk of the collection was returned when the "<i>Staatliche Wirtschaftshochschule Mannheim</i>" (State College of Business Mannheim) was founded. When the business college became a university in 1967, the library acquired new and much expanded collections in all the <a href="/wiki/Course_(education)" title="Course (education)">subjects</a> taught at the university. It also inherited around 240,000 volumes of older books from the "Wissenschaftliche Stadtbibliothek Mannheim" (Scientific Municipal Library Mannheim), which was dissolved in 1970. The library's collection of books and media has nearly doubled since. Today, the University Library of Mannheim maintains four libraries with more than 2.2 million volumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The conventional book supply is complemented by numerous electronic services, such as 30,000 scientific journals, 600 scientific databases and more than 47,000 e-books that can be accessed via e-journal. It is one of Germany's most frequently used library systems and in the German library rankings of 2012, it was placed among the 5 best libraries in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Schloss Ehrenhof</i> library, also known as "<a href="/wiki/Hasso_Plattner" title="Hasso Plattner">Hasso Plattner</a>" library, is located on the Mannheim Palace campus and is the main library of the university. The library was built in 2006 and is among the most modern and best equipped university libraries in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The library's construction was primarily funded by a donation of Euro 10 million by the SAP co-founder Hasso Plattner in 2005. The library was planned by the architects Blocher &amp; Blocher Partners and built by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilfinger_Berger" title="Bilfinger Berger">Bilfinger Berger</a>. Today, on an area of more than 4,700 square meters, the library houses subject-related literature in economics, history, geography and law.</p>
<p>Besides the Hasso Plattner library, there are the business-focused <i>Schloss Schneckenhof</i> library, the humanities-focused <i>A3</i> library and the <i>A5</i> library which has a focus on social sciences, mathematics, computer science and information systems.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg/200px-MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg/300px-MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg/400px-MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MZES_Uni_Mannheim_A5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mannheim Centre for European Social Research (MZES)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The profile of the University of Mannheim is reflected in its research achievements. In economic and social sciences, Mannheim is one of the best research centers in Germany and among the top ten to twenty institutions in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>All disciplines work in close cooperation with each other to determine central research subjects, for example on the topics of decisions, governance, migration and integration or language acquisition.</p>
<p>University of Mannheim's largest research institute is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mannheim_Centre_for_European_Social_Research_(MZES)" title="Mannheim Centre for European Social Research (MZES)">Mannheim Centre for European Social Research</a>. In close collaboration with the School of Social Sciences, it dedicates its research to exploring societal, social and political development in Europe. Focal points are comparative research on Europe and investigating the European integration process.</p>
<p>Furthermore, there are different collaborative research centres, such as SFB 884: "Political Economy of Reforms", which aims to provide scientific insights into success and failure of reforms, determined by competing interests, contexts and the political process of reform-making. The project Group „Contextualized Decision Making: Investigating Mediators and Moderators", funded by the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Forschungsgemeinschaft" title="Deutsche Forschungsgemeinschaft">German Research Foundation (DFG)</a>, investigates how people make decisions and why decisions often depend on weeny aspects of the situation in which they are taken.</p>
<p>There are also a further three renowned research institutes with close ties to the University: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre_for_European_Economic_Research" title="Centre for European Economic Research">ZEW — Centre for European Economic Research</a>, <a href="/wiki/GESIS_%E2%80%93_Leibniz_Institute_for_the_Social_Sciences" title="GESIS – Leibniz Institute for the Social Sciences">GESIS – Leibniz Institute for the Social Sciences</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/IDS_%E2%80%93_Institute_of_German_Language" title="IDS – Institute of German Language">IDS – Institute of German Language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>

<p><b>Mannheim Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation</b><br/>
One of the more recently established institutions that are affiliated with the University is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mannheim_Center_for_Entrepreneurship_and_Innovation_(MCEI)" title="Mannheim Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (MCEI)">Mannheim Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (MCEI)</a> that intends to provide a founder and incubator platform for students, young entrepreneurs and investors. The institute is supported by the Mannheim Institute for Mittelstand and SME Research (IfM) and the Chair of SME Research &amp; Entrepreneurship at the University of Mannheim. Several successful startups have already been launched at the University of Mannheim or been initiated by former students, for instance, <a href="/wiki/Payback_(loyalty_card)" title="Payback (loyalty card)">Payback</a> (€500m exit to <a href="/wiki/American_Express" title="American Express">American Express</a>), <a href="/wiki/Delivery_Hero" title="Delivery Hero">Delivery Hero</a> (raised $1.4b funding),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> <a class="external text" href="https://auto1.com/en/" rel="nofollow">AUTO1 Group</a> (raised $200m funding),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/StudiVZ" title="StudiVZ">StudiVZ</a> (€85m exit to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georg_von_Holtzbrinck_Publishing_Group" title="Georg von Holtzbrinck Publishing Group">Georg von Holtzbrinck Publishing Group</a>), <a href="/wiki/Simfy" title="Simfy">Simfy</a> (raised €30m funding),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Goodgame_Studios" title="Goodgame Studios">Goodgame Studios</a> (initiating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Initial_Public_Offering" title="Initial Public Offering">IPO</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> <a class="external text" href="http://www.savingglobal.com/" rel="nofollow">SavingGlobal</a> (raised $32m funding),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Synchronite (sold to <a href="/wiki/LivePerson" title="LivePerson">LivePerson</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> movilizer (sold to <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> in 2016),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> movilitas (sold to <a class="external text" href="http://www.peak-ryzex.com/" rel="nofollow">Peak-Ryzex</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Amorelie (sold to <a href="/wiki/ProSiebenSat.1_Media" title="ProSiebenSat.1 Media">ProSiebenSat.1 Media</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> <a <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships_and_cooperations">Partnerships and cooperations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Partnerships and cooperations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Mannheim maintains wide-ranging international contacts to universities and organizations on all continents, both in areas of research and student exchange. Apart from being a member of the International Association of Universities (IAU) network, the university participates in several European exchange schemes for researchers and students, such as the European ERASMUS, the IBEA and ENTER programs partnering with universities like <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Stockholm" title="University of Stockholm">University of Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tilburg_University" title="Tilburg University">Tilburg University</a> or <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_University_of_Madrid" title="Charles III University of Madrid">Charles III University of Madrid</a>. It also coordinates several intercontinental projects, mostly through the Erasmus Mundus program. Today, the university maintains more than 550 cooperations with over 400 universities in more than 50 countries and five continents,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> among them:</p>

<p>Besides its direct academic cooperations and exchange programs the University of Mannheim maintains a broad network to other universities and research institutions trough its memberships of the <a href="/wiki/German_Universities_Excellence_Initiative" title="German Universities Excellence Initiative">German Universities Excellence Initiative</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Forschungsgemeinschaft" title="Deutsche Forschungsgemeinschaft">German Research Foundation (DFG)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Quality_Improvement_System" title="European Quality Improvement System">European Quality Improvement System (EQUIS)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Association_to_Advance_Collegiate_Schools_of_Business" title="Association to Advance Collegiate Schools of Business">Association to Advance Collegiate Schools of Business (AACSB)</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_MBAs" title="Association of MBAs">Association of MBAs (AMBA)</a>. Furthermore, Mannheim has set up international summer schools for international students offering (semi-)intensive German courses and numerous subject courses, by the departments of Business Administration and Philosophy.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_Studies">Undergraduate Studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Undergraduate Studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Mannheim is dedicated predominantly to the study and research of social sciences, mathematics and computer sciences and is the only university in the Germany to be so. The UMA awards a range of academic degrees spanning bachelors, masters and PhDs. The postnominals awarded are the degree abbreviations used commonly among German universities.</p>
<p>The University of Mannheim offers a wide variety of academic degrees for undergraduate students. Numerous university rankings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> confirm the excellent status of the overall Mannheim course portfolio. For many years now Mannheim has been recognized as the undisputed top provider of business administration and economics degrees in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wiwo.de_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-wiwo.de-5">[5]</a></sup> The subjects political science,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> sociology,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> history, English studies, Germanic studies, computer science and information systems are also regularly highly ranked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> One of the key features of Mannheim teaching is that as well as the Business School itself, all the other schools offer students the opportunity to acquire substantial business knowledge in addition to their major.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Courses are split across more than thirty research centres and departments, plus a Language Centre (IDS). Since almost all programmes are within the social sciences, they closely resemble each other, and undergraduate as well as graduate students usually take at least one course module in a subject outside of their degree, promoting a broader education in the social sciences. At undergraduate level, specific departments are relatively small (c. 90 students across three years of bachelor studies), ensuring small lecture sizes and a more hands-on approach than other public institutions. Since September 2009, it has been compulsory for second year undergraduates to study Business Ethics alongside normal studies.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_Studies">Graduate Studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Graduate Studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mannheim has a "comprehensive" graduate program with high coexistence with the programs offered to undergraduates. Normally, the University of Mannheim provides further study options for each of its Bachelor programs. The university offers graduate degrees in Master's of Art, Master's of Science, <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Laws" title="Master of Laws">LL.M's</a>, and PhD's in addition to professional degrees such as the Juris Doctor and Master of Business Administration. Admission to graduate programs is decentralized; applicants apply directly to the department or degree program. Most graduate students are supported by fellowships, teach assistantships, or research assistantships. In general, the Master's programs incorporate a strong international dimension, for instance by offering integrated exchange programs and double degrees and an increasing number of them is completely taught in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>The graduate portfolio include:</p>
<table style="width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top; width:50%;">
<ul>
<li>Mannheim Master (M.Sc.) of Management (MMM)</li>
<li>Mannheim Master (M.Sc.) of Finance (available as specialization within MMM)</li>
<li>Mannheim Master (M.Sc.) of Accounting (available as specialization within MMM)</li>
<li>Mannheim Master (M.Sc.) of Marketing (available as specialization within MMM)</li>
<li>Mannheim Master (M.Sc.) in Business Research</li>
<li>Master (LL.M.) of Laws</li>
<li>Master (M.C.B.L.) of Comparative Business Law (also available as joint-degree)</li>
<li>Master (M.Sc.) of Economics</li>
<li>Master (M.Sc.) of Mathematics with Business Administration</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top; width:50%;">
<ul>
<li>Master (M.Sc.) of Computer Science with Business Administration</li>
<li>Mannheim Master (M.Sc.) in Data Science (MMDS)</li>
<li>Master (M.Sc.) of Psychology</li>
<li>Master (M.Sc.) of Sociology</li>
<li>Master (M.A.) in Media &amp; Communication Studies</li>
<li>Master (M.A.) in Language &amp; Communication (also available with Business Administration)</li>
<li>Master (M.A.) in Philosophy (also available with Business Administration)</li>
<li>Master (M.A.) in History (also available with Business Administration)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Staatsexamen" title="Staatsexamen">Staatsexamen (Ref. Jur.)</a> in Law after the <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Laws" title="Bachelor of Laws">LL.B.</a> program</li>
</ul>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mannheim_Business_School.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="588" data-file-width="486" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Mannheim_Business_School.PNG/200px-Mannheim_Business_School.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Mannheim_Business_School.PNG/300px-Mannheim_Business_School.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Mannheim_Business_School.PNG/400px-Mannheim_Business_School.PNG 2x" width="200"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_Graduate_Programs">Joint Graduate Programs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Joint Graduate Programs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MBA" title="MBA">MBA</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Business_School" title="Mannheim Business School">Mannheim Business School</a></li>
<li>Master (M.Sc) of Political Science</li>
<li>Master (M.Sc) of Economics</li>
<li>Master (M.C.B.L.) of Comparative Business Law with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Adelaide" title="University of Adelaide">University of Adelaide</a> (also available as sole Mannheim degree)</li>
<li>International joint MA in Intercultural German Studies (IcGS): Joint degree with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo" title="University of Waterloo">University of Waterloo</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Doctoral_Studies">Doctoral Studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Doctoral Studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mannheim_Graduate_School_for_Economics_and_Social_Sciences" title="Mannheim Graduate School for Economics and Social Sciences">Mannheim Graduate School for Economics and Social Sciences</a> (GESS) provides doctoral training in empirical and quantitative methods and their application to economic and social sciences. The Graduate School is the first of its kind in Germany<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> and is among very few in the world to integrate these disciplines into a coherent curriculum. It is funded by the "Excellence Initiative" of the German government. The GESS consists of the Center Doctoral Studies in Business (CDSB), Center for Doctoral Studies in Economics (CDSE) and the Center for Doctoral Studies in Social and Behavioral Sciences (CDSS).</p>
<p>The GESS offers different PhD programs, among them:</p>
<ul>
<li>Accounting &amp; Taxation</li>
<li>Finance</li>
<li>Management</li>
<li>Marketing</li>
<li>Economics</li>
<li>Political Science</li>
<li>Psychology</li>
<li>Sociology</li>
</ul>
<p>Furthermore, the University of Mannheim offers the possibility to do an individual doctorate which is the traditional option in Germany. Doctoral candidates are supervised by a professor. The School of Humanities offers a third option — in the doctoral training program "Formations of the Global", each doctoral student receives close support from three mentors out of multiple disciplines and is integrated into an interdisciplinary lecture program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_business_education">Continued business education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Continued business education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Mannheim has courses in continued academic education, with the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Business_School" title="Mannheim Business School">Mannheim Business School</a> (MBS) as its prime example. Mannheim Business School is the umbrella organization for continued business education at the University of Mannheim. Programs offered include the Mannheim MBA (different tracks are available, e.g. Asian track), the ESSEC &amp; Mannheim Executive MBA, Tongji &amp; Mannheim Executive MBA and the Master of Accounting &amp; Taxation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StudentsYardUniMa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="622" data-file-width="1015" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/StudentsYardUniMa.jpg/220px-StudentsYardUniMa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/StudentsYardUniMa.jpg/330px-StudentsYardUniMa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/StudentsYardUniMa.jpg/440px-StudentsYardUniMa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StudentsYardUniMa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
UMA students revising on Mannheim's <i>Campuswiese</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mannheim hosts more than 15 <i>Studentenverbindungen</i> (student cooperations), which were predominantly founded in the 19th century. The <i>Studentenverbindungen</i> are to some extent comparable to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fraternities" title="Fraternities">fraternities</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US" title="US">US</a> or <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. As traditional symbols (couleurs) corporation members wear colored caps and ribbons at ceremonial occasions (Kommers) and some of them still practice the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Academic_fencing" title="Academic fencing">academic fencing</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mensur" title="Mensur">Mensur</a></i>), a kind of duelling, with the intention to "shape their members for the challenges of life." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> In the 19th and early 20th century, the <i>Studentenverbindungen</i> played an important role in Germany's student life. Today, however, these corporations include only a relatively small number of students that often have the self-declared mission to keep academic traditions alive and to create friendships for life. The corporations' often representative 19th-century mansions are present throughout Mannheim.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG/200px-Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG/300px-Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG/400px-Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abendliches-Rheinufer-Mannheim-03.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The University of Mannheim campus seen from the shore of <a href="/wiki/Ludwigshafen" title="Ludwigshafen">Ludwigshafen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mannheim is not least famous for its student night life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Besides the various parties regularly organized by the <i>Fachschaften</i> (student councils) of the different faculties, the semester opening and closing parties of the university, the Schlossfest, the dormitory parties, and the soirées of Mannheim's student fraternities, the city, and the metropolitan area even more, offers a wide spectrum of night life activities. Adjacent to Mannheim's main campus is Mannheim <a href="/wiki/Downtown" title="Downtown">downtown</a> that represents the major night life district, where numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bar_(establishment)" title="Bar (establishment)">bars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nightclub" title="Nightclub">clubs</a> are located close to each other. About 10-15 min. by tram away from the Mannheim Palace, Mannheim's upcoming party/pub district <i>Jungbusch</i> can be reached that is also in close neighborhood to several of Mannheim's student resident halls. From Wednesday on, it is all night very crowded and full of atmosphere. Moreover, Mannheim has more than six major clubs. The largest of them, the "Baton Rouge", is located in the middle of downtown adjacent to Mannheim's monument, the <i>Wasserturm</i>. The city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a> - "Germany's finance capitol", which is about three times as large as Mannheim, can be reached a 30-minute train ride away, and offers an even more diverse night life, having a broader variety of clubs and bars. Furthermore, the city of <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg" title="Heidelberg">Heidelberg</a>, that is home to the famous <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a> and the Old Town with origins in the 13th century, can be reached by train in 15 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
