<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2011–12 academic year there were 12,000 full-time students at the University of Mannheim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Of these, approximately 15% of the student body came from abroad. Furthermore, each academic term around 800 incoming exchange students (370 ERASMUS students) choose the University of Mannheim as their exchange institution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In general, the UMA has, together with the exchange body, a highly international student body, with 110 nationalities represented. Additionally, in the 2011 International Student Barometer, a global survey for international students, the University of Mannheim was ranked #1 in Germany for multicultural study environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Mannheim_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Mannheim-141">[141]</a></sup> There is approximately an equal split between genders with 51% men and 49% female students.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_athletics">Sports and athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Sports and athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Students interested in sports can choose from more than seventy disciplines at the Mannheim Institute of Sports – from beginners to top-level. The Mannheim Institute of Sports is a modern-service enterprise within the University of Mannheim supporting athletics and the health of all students and employees at the University of Mannheim and the region. At the moment the institute offers a wide variety of programs with 241 courses in 76 different athletic disciplines and more than 320 hours per week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Most of the courses are offered free of charge. During the academic terms more than 6.000 students participate weekly.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mannheim_Knights.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="543" data-file-width="880" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mannheim_Knights.jpg/230px-Mannheim_Knights.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mannheim_Knights.jpg/345px-Mannheim_Knights.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mannheim_Knights.jpg/460px-Mannheim_Knights.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mannheim_Knights.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
American Football team of the University, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mannheim_Knights&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mannheim Knights (page does not exist)">Mannheim Knights</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Moreover, the University of Mannheim also maintains numerous sports societies that vary widely in their level and scope. Many more popular sports operate several university teams and departmental teams which compete in leagues against other teams within the university. The university offers a broad variety of <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity teams</a>, such as teams in more than 16 different court sports from <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> to <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a>, courses in several different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martial_Arts" title="Martial Arts">Martial Arts</a>, 26 courses in physical fitness and body building, 9 courses in health sports from aquapower to <a href="/wiki/Yoga" title="Yoga">yoga</a>, and groups in 12 different dance styles. In addition, equestrian sports, <a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">Sailing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rowing" title="Rowing">Rowing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ski" title="Ski">Skiing</a> in the Austrian <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_and_Field" title="Track and Field">Track and Field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">Swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">Fencing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">Cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acrobatics" title="Acrobatics">Acrobatics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">Gymnastics</a>, and many more. Mannheim is also host of a large number of successful athlets that compete on national and international level in several disciplines – the majority of these athletes is supported by the Mannheim Sports Scholarship. Supported students include German champions in <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">Handball</a> (2009), <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">Olympic-style Weightlifting</a> (2009), <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a> (2008), <a href="/wiki/Shooting" title="Shooting">Shooting</a> (2009) and <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">Hockey</a> (2012).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>The University of Mannheim and its sports teams also engages in numerous national and international competitions, such as the "European University Rowing Championships", where the University of Mannheim placed 2nd in 2005 finishing ahead of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, or the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=WHU_Euromasters&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="WHU Euromasters (page does not exist)">WHU Euromasters</a> championships at which Mannheim regularly participates in the disciplines of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer">Soccer</a> (male &amp; female), <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relay_Race" title="Relay Race">Relay Race</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">Rowing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheerleading" title="Cheerleading">Cheerleading</a>. Mannheim regularly competes against the <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull" title="Red Bull">Red Bull Student Boat Battle</a>, an annual university sports event initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_GmbH" title="Red Bull GmbH">Red Bull GmbH</a> that takes place in Mannheim and Heidelberg since 2007. During the competition the two universities celebrate their long-established rivalry by competing in the discipline of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_Jousting" title="Water Jousting">Water Jousting</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Furthermore, the University of Mannheim and the <a href="/wiki/WHU-Otto_Beisheim_School_of_Management" title="WHU-Otto Beisheim School of Management">WHU-Otto Beisheim School of Management</a> established the annual rowing race <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=German_MBA_Rowing_Race&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="German MBA Rowing Race (page does not exist)">German MBA Rowing Race</a> in 2006 where the MBA students of the Mannheim Business School and those of the WHU competing against each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Model for the "German MBA Rowing Race" championships is the prestigious duel <a href="/wiki/The_Boat_Race" title="The Boat Race">The Boat Race</a> between the universities <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a>, carried out annually since 1829. The annual rowing competition takes place alternately either at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moselle_(river)" title="Moselle (river)">Moselle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Koblenz" title="Koblenz">Koblenz</a> or at the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> in Mannheim. The race took place outside of those places in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> in 2013 for the first time of its foundation and congregated an audience of several hundred people. For the first time since 2007, Mannheim has won the race in July 2013 and defended the title in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> The detailed nature of the record-keeping over the event's history has many record statistics being carefully monitored. A selection of the more frequently cited statistics includes: Number of wins: WHU, 6; Mannheim, 3 (2006, 2013, 2014); Most consecutive victories: WHU, 6 (2007–2012).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_clubs">Student clubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student clubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:173px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sicor_logo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="129" data-file-width="171" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/Sicor_logo.jpg" width="171"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sicor_logo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
SICoR – Student initiative <a href="/wiki/Club_of_Rome" title="Club of Rome">Club of Rome</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AIESEC_logo_bw.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="400" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AIESEC_logo_bw.png/170px-AIESEC_logo_bw.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AIESEC_logo_bw.png/255px-AIESEC_logo_bw.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AIESEC_logo_bw.png/340px-AIESEC_logo_bw.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AIESEC_logo_bw.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/AIESEC" title="AIESEC">AIESEC</a> Mannheim e.V.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The university supports a number of student groups in various fields of interest. Currently there are around 36 active student <a href="/wiki/Club_(organization)" title="Club (organization)">clubs</a> or "associations" on Mannheim's campus. Among them are the student parliament <a href="/wiki/AStA" title="AStA">AStA</a>, the student councils of the different faculties (<i>Fachschaften</i>), two drama clubs, the university orchestras Collegium Musicum Instrumentale and College Jazz Orchestra, three choirs, six student media groups, eight groups of political parties, a large number of different NGO's such as <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> Student Initiative 1388 Mannheim, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicef" title="Unicef">Unicef</a> Student Initiative, <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a> Mannheim e.V.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Enactus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Enactus (page does not exist)">Enactus</a> Universität Mannheim e.V or the SICoR – Student initiative <a href="/wiki/Club_of_Rome" title="Club of Rome">Club of Rome</a> e.V. Mannheim, several departments of European organizations of students in certain disciplines, numerous clubs dedicated to fostering international relations and cultural exchange such as <a href="/wiki/AIESEC" title="AIESEC">AIESEC</a> Mannheim e.V., <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AEGEE" title="AEGEE">AEGEE</a> Mannheim e.V. or the <a class="external text" href="http://www.visum-mannheim.de/satellite/" rel="nofollow">VISUM Society of International Student Partnerships</a>, one chess club, one literature club, two debate societies, four religion student groups, several <a href="/wiki/Junior_enterprise" title="Junior enterprise">student-run</a> management consulting groups like INTEGRA e.V.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> and various business or economics related student groups such as the financial industries focused IB League Mannheim e.V., Arbeitskreis Börse e.V. and Mannheim Finance &amp; Controlling Club e.V. (MFCC), the marketing driven <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Market_Team&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Market Team (page does not exist)">Market Team</a> Mannheim<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> and MTP – Marketing zwischen Theorie und Praxis e.V.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> or entrepreneurship interested . The largest student initiative at Mannheim's campus is Arbeitskreis Börse – Studenten der Universität Mannheim e.V. (AKB)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> with more than 1,000 active members and several thousand paying alumni members, founded in 1984 and that is focused on connecting students and companies out of capital markets and consulting. Furthermore, Mannheim students have established the student-run congress <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Forum" title="Mannheim Forum">Mannheim Forum</a> in recent years that is dealing with contemporary topics political, economical and business related topics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The official organization of former students of the University of Mannheim is AbsolventUM Uni-Mannheim. With more than 7,000 members and 50 alumni clubs on 4 continents, it is one of Europe's leading associations of its kind and was recognized as the best alumni association in Germany by the <a href="/wiki/Stifterverband_f%C3%BCr_die_Deutsche_Wissenschaft" title="Stifterverband für die Deutsche Wissenschaft">Stifterverband für die Deutsche Wissenschaft</a> in 2001. Since 1993, the club has been reinforcing the alumni's lifelong bonds with the University of Mannheim, as well as the networks among its members, by means of numerous events and information platforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mannheim_Forum">Mannheim Forum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Mannheim Forum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Forum" title="Mannheim Forum">Mannheim Forum</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mafo14.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="113" data-file-width="450" height="55" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mafo14.png/220px-Mafo14.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mafo14.png/330px-Mafo14.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mafo14.png/440px-Mafo14.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mafo14.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo of the Mannheim Forum 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="509" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg/120px-Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg/180px-Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg/240px-Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mannheim_Forum_2014_Pic_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Forum" title="Mannheim Forum">Mannheim Forum</a> 2014 flag in front of the University of Mannheim</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mannheim Forum is an economic <a href="/wiki/Congress" title="Congress">congress</a> organized exclusively by students of the University of Mannheim and is among the largest collegiate events in Germany with more than 500 participants each year. During the Mannheim Forum various events take place on Mannheim's main <a href="/wiki/Campus" title="Campus">campus</a>. Besides topical speeches by renowned people, the participants also have the opportunity to attend the Recruiting Fair, as well as participate in several company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Workshops" title="Workshops">workshops</a>. During the panel discussions the audience can discuss with several top tier personalities from the worlds of <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">politics</a>. Renowned speaker include Frank Mattern (CEO, McKinsey &amp; Co. Germany), <a href="/wiki/Peer_Steinbr%C3%BCck" title="Peer Steinbrück">Peer Steinbrück</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Achleitner" title="Paul Achleitner">Paul Achleitner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Lindner" title="Christian Lindner">Christian Lindner</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6tz_Werner" title="Götz Werner">Götz Werner</a>, Dirk Müller (famous broker, known as "Mister Dax"), <a href="/wiki/Hamed_Abdel-Samad" title="Hamed Abdel-Samad">Hamed Abdel-Samad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahra_Wagenknecht" title="Sahra Wagenknecht">Sahra Wagenknecht</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Plasberg" title="Frank Plasberg">Frank Plasberg</a> etc. Under the topic „Time Questions: Politics, Economy, Society and Science“, the most recent Forum took place, under the patronage of the state Baden-Württemberg and its Minister-President Winfried Kretschmann, from 13th until 15 March 2015 on Mannheim's main campus - the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Palace" title="Mannheim Palace">Mannheim Palace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, the student initiative Mannheim Forum was founded by the three largest student initiatives at Mannheim's campus: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arbeitskreis_B%C3%B6rse_(AKB)" title="Arbeitskreis Börse (AKB)">Arbeitskreis Börse (AKB)</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.mtp.org/mtp-site/regional/mannheim.nsf/id/pa_gs_start.html" rel="nofollow">MTP - The Marketing Initiative</a>, and <a class="external text" href="http://www.polimotion.de/" rel="nofollow">PoliMotion - The Politics Initiative</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The idea and goal behind the initiative was to establish an event that enable participants and students of different branches of study to engage in dynamic dialog with representatives of politics, science and economics about specific issues that are relevant in today's world. The first event organized by the initiative was the panel discussion in 2012 between Mannheim professors of different disciplines and company representatives about the topic "EU - Economic Poliy - Quo Vadis?!". The event received positive responses from both students and participants alike. From then on, the students' aim was to establish this event on a larger scale under the name "Mannheim Forum" as a fixed annual event at the University of Mannheim. The first Mannheim Forum was then conducted in 2013 under the topic of “Resources – 6 Perspectives: Economy, Ethics, Security, Politics, Technology and Startups”, followed by the Mannheim Forum in 2014 centering on the topic "Distribution of Power in the World". The Mannheim Forum 2015 had its focus on "Time Questions: Politics, Economy, Society and Science".</p>
<p>Mannheim Forum is mainly organized by students in their first and second academic term (nevertheless it is open to every student at UMA) bringing in new ideas and fresh perspectives, but are supported and financed by external partners, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Co." title="McKinsey &amp; Co.">McKinsey &amp; Co.</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SAP_AG" title="SAP AG">SAP AG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reckitt_Benckiser" title="Reckitt Benckiser">Reckitt Benckiser</a>, <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Cement" title="Heidelberg Cement">Heidelberg Cement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoffmann-La_Roche" title="Hoffmann-La Roche">Hoffmann-La Roche</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_Business_School" title="Mannheim Business School">Mannheim Business School</a> and alumni - who ensure that knowledge based on experience is used and implemented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Furthermore, the Mannheim Forum holds close cooperations with other student initiatives at the University of Mannheim, like MTP, Arbeitskreis Börse and POLImotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg/200px-Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg/300px-Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg/400px-Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arena_Of_Pop_2007_-_Menschenmenge_-_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Arena of Pop in 2007 on University of Mannheim's Ehrenhof</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Each year the University of Mannheim is host of the <i>Schlossfest</i> (Palace Festival), a festival at which the Mannheim Palace campus is open to visitors and introduces the university to incoming freshmen. During the <i>Schlossfest</i> several events take place that are dealing with themes out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arts" title="Arts">arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>. The science events include live experiments and academic speeches regarding specific subjects, while the arts events include art exhibitions, art workshops, dance acts, museum guides as well as guides through the old, non-public areas within the Mannheim Palace. Furthermore, several live-acts including musicians like <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Naidoo" title="Xavier Naidoo">Xavier Naidoo</a> (2011), <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6hne_Mannheims" title="Söhne Mannheims">Söhne Mannheims</a>, orchestras as well as comedians like <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BClent_Ceylan" title="Bülent Ceylan">Bülent Ceylan</a> (2009) are part of the event program. The Schlossfest in 2013 attracted more than 13,800 visitors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The University of Mannheim also regularly hosts a large number of concerts, sport events, talks as well as theatrical performances. One of the largest events represents the annual music concert <i>Arena of Pop</i> organized by the radio station <a href="/wiki/BigFM" title="BigFM">BigFM</a> that featured acts including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P!nk" title="P!nk">P!nk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreigner_(band)" title="Foreigner (band)">Foreigner</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sunrise_Avenue" title="Sunrise Avenue">Sunrise Avenue</a>.</p>
<p>Besides the <i>Schlossfest</i> the University fosters the long-established tradition of weekly <i>Schneckenhof</i> parties that usually take place Thursdays on UMA's popular <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangle</a> "the Schneckenhof" during the summer terms and in UMA's <a href="/wiki/Catacombs" title="Catacombs">catacombs</a> during the winter terms and that are regularly organized by the <i>Fachschaften</i> (student councils) of the different faculties. The tradition of conducting parties on the Schneckenhof dates back to the early 1990s. Of those parties the most famous are the ones hosted by the <i>Fachschaft BWL</i> (Student Council of Business Administration) once each academic term, called "BWLer Fete", which normally attract the largest number of visitors, e.g. 3,000 in Fall 2013. The BWLer Fete is traditionally sponsored by different corporate partners such as <a href="/wiki/Hays_plc" title="Hays plc">Hays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Wyman" title="Oliver Wyman">Oliver Wyman</a> or <a href="/wiki/MLP_AG" title="MLP AG">MLP</a> and each party is organized under a unique theme, such as Russian Lover (Fall 2010), Circus Circus (Summer 2010), Like A Boss (Fall 2012) or Schneckenhof Goes Hollywood (Fall 2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Each of the "BWLer Fete" parties usually ends with the <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">refrain</a> of the song "Meine Stadt" by the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6hne_Mannheims" title="Söhne Mannheims">Söhne Mannheims</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"<i>Meine Stadt holt ihren Mann Heim,</i> <i>Ganz egal wo er auch ist.</i></p>
<i>Diesen Reim schickt ihr der Mann Heim, Der sie so oft vermisst.</i>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Songtextemania.com_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Songtextemania.com-167">[167]</a></sup></blockquote>
<p>Another event that has become a popular tradition at the University of Mannheim are the <i>Norweger Parties</i> (Norwegian Partys) that were established by <a href="/wiki/Norwegians" title="Norwegians">Norwegian</a> Mannheim alumni in 1981. Normally, the event takes place during the academic summer at the University's Schneckenhof and is organized and hosted by Norwegian exchange students or Mannheim students with Norwegian background, in conjunction with international UMA societies. The event is characterized by attracting a large number of visitors (3,000 in 2013) and belongs to the most popular Schneckenparties. During the event the Schneckenhof is decorated in Norwegian themes and offers traditional beverages and food from Norway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers_and_radio">Newspapers and radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Newspapers and radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Student newspapers include the long-established The UniMAgazin and its younger rival, The ForUM. Together with colleagues from the <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a>, students run a radio station since 2001, <a class="external text" href="https://www.radioaktiv.org/" rel="nofollow">radioaktiv</a>, which provides members with an opportunity to produce and host weekly radio shows and promotes broadcast journalism, sports coverage, comedy and drama.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1150" data-file-width="894" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg/160px-WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg/240px-WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg/320px-WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WohnheimN6Mannheim.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the dormitories reserved for Mannheim students, the Wohnheim N6,8 in downtown Mannheim</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Student Housing – while not directly on-campus – is provided through the "<i>Studentenwerk Mannheim</i>" (Student Services Mannheim) which offers student accommodation and catering services with more than 19 residence halls and 13 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cantinas" title="Cantinas">cantinas</a>. The residence halls have an overall capacity of more than 3,150 places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Furthermore, the "Studentenwerk" also runs a general social counseling service, a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursery_school" title="Nursery school">nursery</a> and other social institutions.</p>
<p>Different apartment types and single rooms in residence halls, traditional working-class neighborhoods or upscale <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">suburbs</a> are available. Most rooms are furnished and hard wired to the university's computer center, which means that internet is for free. The monthly fees also cover heating, hot water and hall cleaning. The prices for a single room ranges between €285–330 per month and €260–380 per month for single apartments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> All the residence halls are within cycling distance to the colleges and are well linked to the vast public transportation network of Mannheim City. The catering services include the operation of the university's canteen and cafeteria EO which are offering meals for students at discounted prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Applications for rooms or apartments in the residence halls can be made online or at "Studentenwerk" help desks at Mannheim's campus. Applications for these sought – after places can be made at any time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>The closest residences to the Mannheim Palace campus are located in the squares L8 and N6. The Hermann-Heimerich-Haus in N6,8 offers 70 units (20 single rooms in two-person apartments and 50 single-person apartments) and maintains a rooftop common room accessible by all residents. It is situated next to Mannheim's shopping malls, the Mannheim main station and the <i>Mannheimer Wasserturm</i>, which is Mannheim's landmark. The residence hall L8, 13+14 offers nine single room apartments and is closest to the university's main campus and in direct neighborhood to the Mannheim Palace. Besides these two close resident halls, several further resident halls in relative short distance to the campus are available with good connections to the public transportation system in Mannheim.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty_members">Notable alumni and faculty members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Mannheim_people" title="List of University of Mannheim people">List of University of Mannheim people</a></div>
<p>Alumni and faculty of the University of Mannheim include many founders and businessmen as well as a large number of internationally acclaimed <a href="/wiki/Economist" title="Economist">economists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philosopher" title="Philosopher">philosophers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurisprudence" title="Jurisprudence">jurisprudents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social scientists</a>. In business, Mannheim alumni and faculty notably founded, co-founded or presided over <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>; <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Re" title="Swiss Re">Swiss Re</a>; <a href="/wiki/Coty,_Inc." title="Coty, Inc.">Coty</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SAP_AG" title="SAP AG">SAP</a>; <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>; <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler</a>; <a href="/wiki/Wild_(company)" title="Wild (company)">WILD</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Boss" title="Hugo Boss">Hugo Boss</a>; <a href="/wiki/Escada" title="Escada">Escada</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bench_(British_clothing_brand)" title="Bench (British clothing brand)">Bench.</a>; <a href="/wiki/K%2BS" title="K+S">K+S</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evonik" title="Evonik">Evonik</a>; <a href="/wiki/TAG_Tegernsee_Immobilien_und_Beteiligung" title="TAG Tegernsee Immobilien und Beteiligung">TAG AG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a>. Alumni and faculty in the field of <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a> include the President of the <a href="/wiki/Ifo_Institute_for_Economic_Research" title="Ifo Institute for Economic Research">Ifo Institute for Economic Research</a> <a href="/wiki/Hans-Werner_Sinn" title="Hans-Werner Sinn">Hans-Werner Sinn</a>, the former President of the <a href="/wiki/German_Institute_for_Economic_Research" title="German Institute for Economic Research">DIW Berlin</a> Klaus F. Zimmermann, the President of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZEW" title="ZEW">ZEW</a> <a href="/wiki/Clemens_Fuest" title="Clemens Fuest">Clemens Fuest</a>, the President of the <a href="/wiki/RWI_Essen" title="RWI Essen">RWI Essen</a> <a href="/wiki/Christoph_M._Schmidt" title="Christoph M. Schmidt">Christoph M. Schmidt</a>, economists <a href="/wiki/Axel_Dreher" title="Axel Dreher">Axel Dreher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Schnabel" title="Isabel Schnabel">Isabel Schnabel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horst_Siebert" title="Horst Siebert">Horst Siebert</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Wilhelm_Leibniz_Prize" title="Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz Prize">Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz Prize</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Roman_Inderst" title="Roman Inderst">Roman Inderst</a> and <a href="/wiki/Knut_Borchardt" title="Knut Borchardt">Knut Borchardt</a>. Alumni in the field of computer science include the Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz Prize winners <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Weickert" title="Joachim Weickert">Joachim Weickert</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Daniel_Cremers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Daniel Cremers (page does not exist)">Daniel Cremers</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Hans_Meuer" title="Hans Meuer">Hans Meuer</a>, chairman of the <a href="/wiki/International_Supercomputing_Conference" title="International Supercomputing Conference">International Supercomputing Conference</a>. With a current network of more than 80,000 living alumni, the University of Mannheim is one of the most influential business institutions in Germany. Among former students, many have reached top positions in business, -including in <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a> companies-, and in politics.</p>

<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Mannheim&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<ul>
<li>Gaugler, Eduard. Die Universität Mannheim in Vergangenheit und Gegenwart, Mannheim, 1976. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783874550437">ISBN 978-3-874-55043-7</a></li>
<li>Enzenauer, Markus. Wirtschaftsgeschichte in Mannheim, Mannheim, 2005. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783938031131">ISBN 978-3-938-03113-1</a></li>
<li>AStA der Universität Mannheim. Was nicht im Rektoratsbericht stand: Wirtschaftshochschule, Universität Mannheim geheim: Annotationen zur Geschichte der Wirtschaftshochschule/Universität Mannheim im Kalten Krieg und danach, Universität Mannheim: Schriftenreihe des AStA der Universität Mannheim; Bd.</li>
<li>Degner, Marius. Entwicklung von Professuren im Fach Betriebswirtschaftslehre, Universität Mannheim: Forschungsberichte / Universität Mannheim, Fakultät für Betriebswirtschaftslehre, Mannheim, 2009. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/search?fq=x0:jrnl&amp;q=n2:0340-1650" rel="nofollow">0340-1650</a></li>
<li>Hamann, Horst. Universität Mannheim, Ed Panorama, Mannheim, 2007. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783898233309">ISBN 978-3-89823-330-9</a></li>
<li>Grüb, Birgit. Gründung von Universitätsverlagen am Beispiel der Universität Mannheim, Mannheim Univ. Press, Mannheim, 2006. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783939352013">ISBN 978-3-939352-01-3</a></li>
<li>Bauer, Gerhard; Budde, Kai; Kreutz, Wilhelm; Schäfer, Patrick. (Published for Academia Domitor - Studienforum Johann Jakob Hemmer e.V.): „Di fernunft siget“. Der kurpfälzische Universalgelehrte Johann Jakob Hemmer (1733-1790) und sein Werk (= Jahrbuch für internationale Germanistik. Reihe A, Kongressberichte, Band 103). Peter Lang, Bern 2010, p. 149–174. Online. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783034304450">ISBN 978-3-0343-0445-0</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Eid" title="Ludwig Eid">Eid, Ludwig</a>. Die gelehrten Gesellschaften der Pfalz, Verlag der Jägerschen Buchhandlung, Speyer, 1926.</li>
<li>Ebersold, Guenther. Rokoko, Reform und Revolution. Ein politisches Lebensbild des Kurfürsten Karl Theodor. Frankfurt a. M. 1985. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783820454864">ISBN 978-3820454-86-4</a></li>
<li>Fuchs, Peter. Kurfürst Karl Theodor von Pfalzbayern (1724−1799). In: Pfälzer Lebensbilder, Publisher. Kurt Baumann, Band 3, Speyer 1977, p. 65−105.</li>
<li>Mörz, Stefan. Aufgeklärter Absolutismus in der Kurpfalz während der Mannheimer Regierungszeit des Kurfürsten Karl Theodor 1742−77. Stuttgart 1991. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783170111868">ISBN 978-3-1701118-68</a></li>
</ul>
